The Philippines, Vietnam, Malaysia, Brunei, Indonesia, and Singapore, have integral rivers that flow into the South China Sea.\n</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mayon_Volcano" title="Mayon Volcano">Mayon Volcano</a>, despite being dangerously <a href="/wiki/List_of_active_volcanoes_in_the_Philippines" title="List of active volcanoes in the Philippines">active</a>, holds the record of the world\'s most perfect cone which is built from past and continuous <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eruption" title="Eruption">eruption</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Davis_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-Davis-91">[91]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Boundaries">Boundaries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Southeast_Asia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Boundaries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Austronesia" title="Austronesia">Austronesia</a></div>\n<p>Southeast Asia is bounded to the southeast by the <a href="/wiki/Australia_(continent)" title="Australia (continent)">Australian continent</a>, a boundary which runs through Indonesia. But a cultural touch point lies between <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea" title="Papua New Guinea">Papua New Guinea</a> and the Indonesian region of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Papua_(Indonesian_province)" title="Papua (Indonesian province)">Papua</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/West_Papua_(Indonesian_province)" title="West Papua (Indonesian province)">West Papua</a>, which shares the island of <a href="/wiki/New_Guinea" title="New Guinea">New Guinea</a> with Papua New Guinea.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Southeast_Asia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Southeast_Asia_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1460" data-file-width="1900" decoding="async" height="169" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Southeast_Asia_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/220px-Southeast_Asia_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Southeast_Asia_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/330px-Southeast_Asia_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Southeast_Asia_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/440px-Southeast_Asia_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Southeast_Asia_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Southeast Asia map of K&#246;ppen climate classification.</div></div></div>\n<p>The climate in Southeast Asia is mainly tropical&#8211;hot and humid all year round with plentiful rainfall. Northern Vietnam and the Myanmar Himalayas are the only regions in Southeast Asia that feature a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Subtropical_climate" title="Subtropical climate">subtropical climate</a>, which has a cold winter with snow. The majority of Southeast Asia has a wet and dry season caused by seasonal shift in winds or <a href="/wiki/Monsoon" title="Monsoon">monsoon</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Tropical_rain_belt" title="Tropical rain belt">tropical rain belt</a> causes additional rainfall during the monsoon season. The rain forest is the second largest on earth (with the Amazon being the largest). An exception to this type of climate and vegetation is the mountain areas in the northern region, where high altitudes lead to milder temperatures and drier landscape. Other parts fall out of this climate because they are desert like. Climate change will have a big effect on agriculture in Southeast Asia such as irrigation systems will be affected by changes in rainfall and runoff, and subsequently, water quality and supply.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environment">Environment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Southeast_Asia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Environment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asian_coral_reefs" title="Southeast Asian coral reefs">Southeast Asian coral reefs</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wallace_line" title="Wallace line">Wallace line</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Komodo_dragon_at_Komodo_National_Park.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="533" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Komodo_dragon_at_Komodo_National_Park.jpg/220px-Komodo_dragon_at_Komodo_National_Park.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Komodo_dragon_at_Komodo_National_Park.jpg/330px-Komodo_dragon_at_Komodo_National_Park.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Komodo_dragon_at_Komodo_National_Park.jpg/440px-Komodo_dragon_at_Komodo_National_Park.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Komodo_dragon_at_Komodo_National_Park.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Komodo dragon in <a href="/wiki/Komodo_National_Park" title="Komodo National Park">Komodo National Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The vast majority of Southeast Asia falls within the warm, humid tropics, and its climate generally can be characterised as monsoonal.\nThe animals of Southeast Asia are diverse; on the islands of <a href="/wiki/Borneo" title="Borneo">Borneo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sumatra" title="Sumatra">Sumatra</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Orangutan" title="Orangutan">orangutan</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Asian_elephant" title="Asian elephant">Asian elephant</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Malayan_tapir" title="Malayan tapir">Malayan tapir</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Sumatran_rhinoceros" title="Sumatran rhinoceros">Sumatran rhinoceros</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Bornean_clouded_leopard" title="Bornean clouded leopard">Bornean clouded leopard</a> can also be found. Six subspecies of the <a href="/wiki/Binturong" title="Binturong">binturong</a> or <i>bearcat</i> exist in the region, though the one endemic to the island of <a href="/wiki/Palawan" title="Palawan">Palawan</a> is now classed as vulnerable.\n</p><p>Tigers of three different subspecies are found on the island of Sumatra (the Sumatran tiger), in peninsular Malaysia (the Malayan tiger), and in Indochina (the Indochinese tiger); all of which are endangered species.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Komodo_dragon" title="Komodo dragon">Komodo dragon</a> is the largest living species of lizard and inhabits the islands of <a href="/wiki/Komodo_(island)" title="Komodo (island)">Komodo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rinca" title="Rinca">Rinca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Flores" title="Flores">Flores</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Gili_Motang" title="Gili Motang">Gili Motang</a> in Indonesia.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pithecophaga_jefferyi.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="477" data-file-width="388" decoding="async" height="209" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Pithecophaga_jefferyi.jpg/170px-Pithecophaga_jefferyi.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Pithecophaga_jefferyi.jpg/255px-Pithecophaga_jefferyi.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Pithecophaga_jefferyi.jpg/340px-Pithecophaga_jefferyi.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pithecophaga_jefferyi.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Philippine_eagle" title="Philippine eagle">Philippine eagle</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Philippine_eagle" title="Philippine eagle">Philippine eagle</a> is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_bird" title="National bird">national bird</a> of the Philippines. It is considered by scientists as the largest eagle in the world,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> and is endemic to the Philippines\' forests.\n</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wild_Asian_water_buffalo" title="Wild Asian water buffalo">wild Asian water buffalo</a>, and on various islands related dwarf species of <i><a href="/wiki/Bubalus" title="Bubalus">Bubalus</a></i> such as <a href="/wiki/Anoa" title="Anoa">anoa</a> were once widespread in Southeast Asia; nowadays the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Domestic_Asian_water_buffalo" title="Domestic Asian water buffalo">domestic Asian water buffalo</a> is common across the region, but its remaining relatives are rare and endangered.\n</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mouse_deer" title="Mouse deer">mouse deer</a>, a small tusked deer as large as a toy dog or cat, mostly can be found on Sumatra, Borneo (Indonesia) and in Palawan Islands (Philippines). The <a href="/wiki/Gaur" title="Gaur">gaur</a>, a gigantic wild ox larger than even wild water buffalo, is found mainly in Indochina. There is very little scientific information available regarding Southeast Asian amphibians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Birds such as the <a href="/wiki/Peafowl" title="Peafowl">peafowl</a> and <a href="/wiki/Drongo" title="Drongo">drongo</a> live in this subregion as far east as Indonesia. The <a href="/wiki/Babirusa" title="Babirusa">babirusa</a>, a four-tusked pig, can be found in Indonesia as well. The <a href="/wiki/Hornbill" title="Hornbill">hornbill</a> was prized for its beak and used in trade with China. The horn of the rhinoceros, not part of its skull, was prized in China as well.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Malay_Archipelago" title="Malay Archipelago">Indonesian Archipelago</a> is split by the <a href="/wiki/Wallace_Line" title="Wallace Line">Wallace Line</a>. This line runs along what is now known to be a tectonic plate boundary, and separates Asian (Western) species from Australasian (Eastern) species. The islands between Java/Borneo and Papua form a mixed zone, where both types occur, known as Wallacea. As the pace of development accelerates and populations continue to expand in Southeast Asia, concern has increased regarding the impact of human activity on the region\'s environment. A significant portion of Southeast Asia, however, has not changed greatly and remains an unaltered home to wildlife. The nations of the region, with only few exceptions, have become aware of the need to maintain forest cover not only to prevent <a href="/wiki/Soil_erosion" title="Soil erosion">soil erosion</a> but to preserve the diversity of flora and fauna. Indonesia, for example, has created an extensive system of national parks and preserves for this purpose. Even so, such species as the <a href="/wiki/Javan_rhinoceros" title="Javan rhinoceros">Javan rhinoceros</a> face extinction, with only a handful of the animals remaining in western Java.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wallace%27s_line.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="488" data-file-width="728" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Wallace%27s_line.jpg/220px-Wallace%27s_line.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Wallace%27s_line.jpg/330px-Wallace%27s_line.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Wallace%27s_line.jpg/440px-Wallace%27s_line.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wallace%27s_line.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Wallace\'s hypothetical line divide Indonesian Archipelago into 2 types of fauna, Australasian and Southeast Asian fauna. The deep water of the <a href="/wiki/Lombok_Strait" title="Lombok Strait">Lombok Strait</a> between the islands of <a href="/wiki/Bali" title="Bali">Bali</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lombok" title="Lombok">Lombok</a> formed a water barrier even when lower sea levels linked the now-separated islands and landmasses on either side.</div></div></div>\n<p>The shallow waters of the <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asian_coral_reefs" title="Southeast Asian coral reefs">Southeast Asian coral reefs</a> have the highest levels of <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity" title="Biodiversity">biodiversity</a> for the world\'s marine ecosystems, where coral, fish and molluscs abound. According to Conservation International, marine surveys suggest that the marine life diversity in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Raja_Ampat" title="Raja Ampat">Raja Ampat</a> (Indonesia) is the highest recorded on Earth. Diversity is considerably greater than any other area sampled in the Coral Triangle composed of Indonesia, Philippines, and Papua New Guinea. The Coral Triangle is the heart of the world\'s coral reef biodiversity, the Verde Passage is dubbed by Conservation International as the world\'s "center of the center of marine shorefish biodiversity". The <a href="/wiki/Whale_shark" title="Whale shark">whale shark</a>, the world\'s largest species of fish and 6 species of <a href="/wiki/Sea_turtle" title="Sea turtle">sea turtles</a> can also be found in the <a href="/wiki/South_China_Sea" title="South China Sea">South China Sea</a> and the Pacific Ocean territories of the Philippines.\n</p><p>The trees and other plants of the region are tropical; in some countries where the mountains are tall enough, temperate-climate vegetation can be found. These rainforest areas are currently being logged-over, especially in Borneo.\n</p><p>While Southeast Asia is rich in flora and fauna, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Deforestation_in_Southeast_Asia" title="Deforestation in Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia is facing severe deforestation</a> which causes habitat loss for various <a href="/wiki/Endangered_species" title="Endangered species">endangered species</a> such as orangutan and the <a href="/wiki/Sumatran_tiger" title="Sumatran tiger">Sumatran tiger</a>. Predictions have been made that more than 40% of the animal and <a href="/wiki/Flora" title="Flora">plant species</a> in Southeast Asia could be wiped out in the 21st century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> At the same time, <a href="/wiki/Haze" title="Haze">haze</a> has been a regular occurrence. The two worst regional hazes were in <a href="/wiki/1997_Southeast_Asian_haze" title="1997 Southeast Asian haze">1997</a> and <a href="/wiki/2006_Southeast_Asian_haze" title="2006 Southeast Asian haze">2006</a> in which multiple countries were covered with thick haze, mostly caused by "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slash_and_burn" title="Slash and burn">slash and burn</a>" activities in Sumatra and Borneo. In reaction, several countries in Southeast Asia signed the <a href="/wiki/ASEAN_Agreement_on_Transboundary_Haze_Pollution" title="ASEAN Agreement on Transboundary Haze Pollution">ASEAN Agreement on Transboundary Haze Pollution</a> to combat haze pollution.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/2013_Southeast_Asian_haze" title="2013 Southeast Asian haze">2013 Southeast Asian Haze</a> saw API levels reach a hazardous level in some countries. Muar experienced the highest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Air_pollution_index" title="Air pollution index">API</a> level of 746 on 23 June 2013 at around 7 am.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Southeast_Asia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_port_of_Singapore.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="843" data-file-width="1260" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/The_port_of_Singapore.jpg/220px-The_port_of_Singapore.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/The_port_of_Singapore.jpg/330px-The_port_of_Singapore.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/The_port_of_Singapore.jpg/440px-The_port_of_Singapore.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_port_of_Singapore.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Singapore" title="Port of Singapore">Port of Singapore</a> is the busiest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_world%27s_busiest_transshipment_ports" title="List of world\'s busiest transshipment ports">transshipment</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_busiest_container_ports" title="List of busiest container ports">container port</a> in the world, and is an important transportation and shipping hub in Southeast Asia.</div></div></div>\n<p>Even prior to the penetration of European interests, Southeast Asia was a critical part of the world trading system. A wide range of commodities originated in the region, but especially important were spices such as pepper, ginger, cloves, and nutmeg. The spice trade initially was developed by <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">Indian</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arab" title="Arab">Arab</a> merchants, but it also brought Europeans to the region. First <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spaniards</a> (<a href="/wiki/Manila_galleon" title="Manila galleon">Manila galleon</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Portugal" title="Kingdom of Portugal">Portuguese</a>, then the Dutch, and finally the British and French became involved in this enterprise in various countries. The penetration of European commercial interests gradually evolved into annexation of territories, as traders lobbied for an extension of control to protect and expand their activities. As a result, the Dutch moved into <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>, the British into <a href="/wiki/Malay_Peninsula" title="Malay Peninsula">Malaya</a> and parts of Borneo, the French into <a href="/wiki/Indochina" title="Indochina">Indochina</a>, and the Spanish and the US into the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>. An economic effect of this imperialism was the shift in the production of commodities. For example, the rubber plantations of Malaysia, Java, Vietnam and Cambodia, the tin mining of Malaya, the rice fields of the Mekong Delta in Vietnam and Irrawaddy River delta in Burma, were a response to powerful market demands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Overseas_Chinese" title="Overseas Chinese">overseas Chinese</a> community has played a large role in the development of the economies in the region. The origins of Chinese influence can be traced to the 16th century, when Chinese migrants from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Southern_China" title="Southern China">southern China</a> settled in Indonesia, Thailand, and other Southeast Asian countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Weidenbaum2328_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-Weidenbaum2328-98">[98]</a></sup> Chinese populations in the region saw a rapid increase following the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Communist_Revolution" title="Communist Revolution">Communist Revolution</a> in 1949, which forced many refugees to emigrate outside of China.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Weidenbaum_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-Weidenbaum-99">[99]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The region\'s economy greatly depends on agriculture; rice and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rubber" title="Rubber">rubber</a> have long been prominent exports. Manufacturing and services are becoming more important. An <a href="/wiki/Emerging_market" title="Emerging market">emerging market</a>, Indonesia is the largest economy in this region. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Newly_industrialised_countries" title="Newly industrialised countries">Newly industrialised countries</a> include Indonesia, Malaysia, Thailand, and the Philippines, while Singapore and Brunei are affluent <a href="/wiki/Developed_country" title="Developed country">developed</a> economies. The rest of Southeast Asia is still heavily dependent on agriculture, but Vietnam is notably making steady progress in developing its industrial sectors. The region notably manufactures textiles, electronic high-tech goods such as microprocessors and heavy industrial products such as automobiles. <a href="/wiki/Oil_reserves_in_Southeast_Asia" title="Oil reserves in Southeast Asia">Oil reserves in Southeast Asia</a> are plentiful.\n</p><p>Seventeen telecommunications companies contracted to build the <a href="/wiki/Asia-America_Gateway" title="Asia-America Gateway">Asia-America Gateway</a> submarine cable to connect Southeast Asia to the US<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> This is to avoid disruption of the kind recently caused by the cutting of the undersea cable from Taiwan to the US in the <a href="/wiki/2006_Hengchun_earthquakes" title="2006 Hengchun earthquakes">2006 Hengchun earthquakes</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Island_off_Otres_Beach_Sihanoukville,_Cambodia.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="5184" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Island_off_Otres_Beach_Sihanoukville%2C_Cambodia.jpg/220px-Island_off_Otres_Beach_Sihanoukville%2C_Cambodia.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Island_off_Otres_Beach_Sihanoukville%2C_Cambodia.jpg/330px-Island_off_Otres_Beach_Sihanoukville%2C_Cambodia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Island_off_Otres_Beach_Sihanoukville%2C_Cambodia.jpg/440px-Island_off_Otres_Beach_Sihanoukville%2C_Cambodia.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Island_off_Otres_Beach_Sihanoukville,_Cambodia.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Along with its temples Cambodia has been promoting its coastal resorts.Island off Otres Beach Sihanoukville, Cambodia.</div></div></div>\n<p>Tourism has been a key factor in economic development for many Southeast Asian countries, especially Cambodia. According to UNESCO, "tourism, if correctly conceived, can be a tremendous development tool and an effective means of preserving the cultural diversity of our planet."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> Since the early 1990s, "even the non-ASEAN nations such as Cambodia, Laos, Vietnam and Burma, where the income derived from tourism is low, are attempting to expand their own tourism industries."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> In 1995, Singapore was the regional leader in tourism receipts relative to GDP at over 8%. By 1998, those receipts had dropped to less than 6% of GDP while Thailand and Lao PDR increased receipts to over 7%. Since 2000, Cambodia has surpassed all other ASEAN countries and generated almost 15% of its GDP from tourism in 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a> is the only member of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/G-20_major_economies" title="G-20 major economies">G-20 major economies</a> and is the largest economy in the region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> Indonesia\'s estimated gross domestic product for 2016 was US$932.4 billion (nominal) or $3,031.3 billion (PPP) with per capita GDP of US$3,604 (nominal) or $11,717 (PPP).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Stock markets in Southeast Asia have performed better than other bourses in the Asia-Pacific region in 2010, with the Philippines\' <a href="/wiki/PSE_Composite_Index" title="PSE Composite Index">PSE</a> leading the way with 22 percent growth, followed by Thailand\'s <a href="/wiki/SET_Index" title="SET Index">SET</a> with 21 percent and Indonesia\'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/JSX_Composite" title="JSX Composite">JKSE</a> with 19 percent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Southeast Asia\'s GDP per capita is US$3,853 according to a 2015 United Nations report, which is comparable to Guatemala and Tonga.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable sortable">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Country\n</th>\n<th><a population">Population</a><br/>(2017)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Population_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-Population-109">[109]</a></sup>\n</th>\n<th><a capita</a><br/>(2017)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:12_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-:12-111">[111]</a></sup>\n</th>\n<th><a href="/wiki/Economic_growth" title="Economic growth">GDP composition">Main industries</a>\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="720" data-file-width="1440" decoding="async" height="12" <a href="/wiki/Brunei_dollar" title="Brunei dollar">Brunei dollar</a>\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:right">443,593\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:right">$12.743 billion\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:right">$29,712\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:right">0.5%\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:right">-0.1%\n</td>\n<td>Petroleum, Petrochemicals, Fishing\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="400" data-file-width="625" decoding="async" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Flag_of_Cambodia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Cambodia.svg.png" class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Southeast_Asia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Southeast_Asia_population_distribution.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="590" data-file-width="921" decoding="async" height="141" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Southeast_Asia_population_distribution.png/220px-Southeast_Asia_population_distribution.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Southeast_Asia_population_distribution.png/330px-Southeast_Asia_population_distribution.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Southeast_Asia_population_distribution.png/440px-Southeast_Asia_population_distribution.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Southeast_Asia_population_distribution.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Population distribution of the countries of Southeast Asia (with Indonesia split into its major islands).</div></div></div>\n<p>Southeast Asia has an area of approximately {{convert|4500000|km2|mi2}]. As of 2016, around 642 million people live in the region, more than a fifth live (143&#160;million) on the Indonesian island of <a href="/wiki/Java" title="Java">Java</a>, the most densely populated large island in the world. <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a> is the most populous country with 261 million people, and also the 4th most populous country in the world. The distribution of the religions and people is diverse in Southeast Asia and varies by country. Some 30&#160;million <a href="/wiki/Overseas_Chinese" title="Overseas Chinese">overseas Chinese</a> also live in Southeast Asia, most prominently in <a href="/wiki/Christmas_Island" title="Christmas Island">Christmas Island</a>, Indonesia, Malaysia, the Philippines, Singapore, and Thailand, and also as the <a href="/wiki/Hoa_people" title="Hoa people">Hoa</a> in Vietnam. People of Southeast Asian origins are known as Southeast Asians or Aseanites.\n</p><p><br/>\n</p>\n<table class="navbox">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th class="navbox-title" colspan="10"><div style="float:right; href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">1,561,959\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:center;background:#f0f0f0;">10</td>\n<td Lumpur</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">1,475,337\n</td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">Ethnic groups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Southeast_Asia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Ethnic groups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_of_Southeast_Asia" title="Ethnic groups of Southeast Asia">Ethnic groups of Southeast Asia</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ati_woman.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="567" data-file-width="630" decoding="async" height="198" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Ati_woman.jpg/220px-Ati_woman.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Ati_woman.jpg/330px-Ati_woman.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Ati_woman.jpg/440px-Ati_woman.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ati_woman.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ati_(tribe)" title="Ati (tribe)">Ati</a> woman in <a href="/wiki/Aklan" title="Aklan">Aklan</a>&#160;&#8211; the <a href="/wiki/Negrito" title="Negrito">Negritos</a> were the earliest inhabitants of Southeast Asia</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Orang_Asli" title="Orang Asli">Aslians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Negrito" title="Negrito">Negritos</a> were believed as one of the earliest inhabitant in the region. They are genetically related to the <a href="/wiki/Papuan_people" title="Papuan people">Papuans</a> in Eastern Indonesia and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Australian_Aborigines" title="Australian Aborigines">Australian Aborigines</a>. The next waves of human migration to Southeast Asia were <a href="/wiki/Austroasiatic_languages" title="Austroasiatic languages">Austroasiatic</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Austronesians" title="Austronesians">Austronesians</a>, which today forming the majority of the regional population.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p><p>In modern times, the <a href="/wiki/Javanese_people" title="Javanese people">Javanese</a> are the largest ethnic group in Southeast Asia, with more than 100 million people, mostly concentrated in <a href="/wiki/Java" title="Java">Java</a>, Indonesia. The second largest ethnic group in Southeast Asia is <a href="/wiki/Vietnamese_people" title="Vietnamese people">Vietnamese</a> with around 86 million population, mainly inhabit Vietnam forming significant minority in neighboring Cambodia and Laos. The <a href="/wiki/Thai_people" title="Thai people">Thais</a> is also a significant ethnic group with around 59 million population forming the majority in Thailand. In Burma, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bamar" title="Bamar">Burmese</a> account for more than two-thirds of the ethnic stock in this country. \n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bali_%E2%80%93_The_People_(2685069056).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1102" data-file-width="833" decoding="async" height="291" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Bali_%E2%80%93_The_People_%282685069056%29.jpg/220px-Bali_%E2%80%93_The_People_%282685069056%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Bali_%E2%80%93_The_People_%282685069056%29.jpg/330px-Bali_%E2%80%93_The_People_%282685069056%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Bali_%E2%80%93_The_People_%282685069056%29.jpg/440px-Bali_%E2%80%93_The_People_%282685069056%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bali_%E2%80%93_The_People_(2685069056).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Native_Indonesian" title="Native Indonesian">Native Indonesian</a> <a href="/wiki/Balinese_people" title="Balinese people">Balinese</a> girl wearing <a href="/wiki/Kebaya" title="Kebaya">kebaya</a> during a traditional ceremony.</div></div></div>\n<p>Indonesia is clearly dominated by the <a href="/wiki/Javanese_people" title="Javanese people">Javanese</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sundanese_people" title="Sundanese people">Sundanese</a> ethnic groups, with hundreds of ethnic minorities inhabited the archipelago, including <a href="/wiki/Madurese_people" title="Madurese people">Madurese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Minangkabau_people" title="Minangkabau people">Minangkabau</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bugis" title="Bugis">Bugis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Balinese_people" title="Balinese people">Balinese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dayak_people" title="Dayak people">Dayak</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Batak_(Indonesia)" title="Batak (Indonesia)">Batak</a> and <a href="/wiki/Malay_Indonesian" title="Malay Indonesian">Malays</a>. While Malaysia is split between more than half <a href="/wiki/Malaysian_Malay" title="Malaysian Malay">Malays</a> and one-quarter Chinese, and also Indian minority in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/West_Malaysia" title="West Malaysia">West Malaysia</a> however <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dayaks" title="Dayaks">Dayaks</a> is the most majority in <a href="/wiki/Sarawak" title="Sarawak">Sarawak</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kadazan-dusun" title="Kadazan-dusun">Kadazan-dusun</a> is the most majority in <a href="/wiki/Sabah" title="Sabah">Sabah</a> which are in the <a href="/wiki/East_Malaysia" title="East Malaysia">East Malaysia</a>. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ethnic_Malay" title="Ethnic Malay">Malays</a> are the majority in West Malaysia and Brunei, while they forming a significant minority in <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thai_Malay" title="Thai Malay">Southern Thailand</a>, <a href="/wiki/East_Malaysia" title="East Malaysia">East Malaysia</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Malay_Singaporean" title="Malay Singaporean">Singapore</a>. In city-state Singapore, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese_Singaporean" title="Chinese Singaporean">Chinese</a> are the majority, yet the city is a multicultural melting pot with Malays, Indians and Eurasian also called the island their home.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Chams" title="Chams">Chams</a> forming a significant minority in Central and South Vietnam, also in Central Cambodia. While the <a href="/wiki/Khmer_people" title="Khmer people">Khmers</a> are the majority in Cambodia, and forming a significant minority in <a href="/wiki/Khmer_Krom" title="Khmer Krom">Southern Vietnam</a> and Thailand. The <a href="/wiki/Hmong_people" title="Hmong people">Hmong people</a> are the minority in Vietnam, China and Laos.\n</p><p>Within the Philippines, the  <a href="/wiki/Tagalog_people" title="Tagalog people">Tagalog</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Visayan_people" title="Visayan people">Visayan</a> (mainly <a href="/wiki/Cebuano_people" title="Cebuano people">Cebuanos</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hiligaynon_people" title="Hiligaynon people">Hiligaynons</a>),  <a href="/wiki/Ilocano_people" title="Ilocano people">Ilocano</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bicolano_people" title="Bicolano people">Bicolano</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moro_people" title="Moro people">Moro</a> (mainly <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tausug_people" title="Tausug people">Tausug</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maranao_people" title="Maranao people">Maranao</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Maguindanao_people" title="Maguindanao people">Maguindanao</a>) and Central Luzon (mainly <a href="/wiki/Kapampangan_people" title="Kapampangan people">Kapampangan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pangasinan_people" title="Pangasinan people">Pangasinan</a>) groups are significant.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Southeast_Asia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Buddhism_in_Southeast_Asia" title="Buddhism in Southeast Asia">Buddhism in Southeast Asia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hinduism_in_Southeast_Asia" title="Hinduism in Southeast Asia">Hinduism in Southeast Asia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Southeast_Asia" title="Islam in Southeast Asia">Islam in Southeast Asia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shenism_in_Southeast_Asia" title="Shenism in Southeast Asia">Shenism in Southeast Asia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Muslim_Southeast_Asia" title="Muslim Southeast Asia">Muslim Southeast Asia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_Asia" title="Christianity in Asia">Christianity in Asia</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ac.buddhists.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" title="Thailand">Thailand</a>.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Luang_Prabang_Monks_Alm_Dawn_01.jpg"><img class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wamena_Church_Betlehem.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1397" href="/wiki/File:Wamena_Church_Betlehem.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestant" title="Protestant">Protestant</a> church in <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>. Indonesia has the largest <a href="/wiki/Protestantism_in_Indonesia" title="Protestantism in Indonesia">Protestant population</a> in Southeast Asia.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Besakih_Bali_Indonesia_Pura-Besakih-02.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3840" data-file-width="5760" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Besakih_Bali_Indonesia_Pura-Besakih-02.jpg/220px-Besakih_Bali_Indonesia_Pura-Besakih-02.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Besakih_Bali_Indonesia_Pura-Besakih-02.jpg/330px-Besakih_Bali_Indonesia_Pura-Besakih-02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Besakih_Bali_Indonesia_Pura-Besakih-02.jpg/440px-Besakih_Bali_Indonesia_Pura-Besakih-02.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Besakih_Bali_Indonesia_Pura-Besakih-02.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mother_Temple_of_Besakih" title="Mother Temple of Besakih">Mother Temple of Besakih</a>, one of <a href="/wiki/Bali" title="Bali">Bali</a>\'s most significant <a href="/wiki/Balinese_Hinduism" title="Balinese Hinduism">Balinese Hindu</a> temples.</div></div></div>\n<p>Countries in Southeast Asia practice many different religions. By population, <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> is the most practised faith, numbering approximately 240 million adherents, or about 40% of the entire population, concentrated in <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brunei" title="Brunei">Brunei</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Southern_Thailand" title="Southern Thailand">Southern Thailand</a> and in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Southern_Philippines" title="Southern Philippines">Southern Philippines</a>. Indonesia is the most populous Muslim-majority country around the world.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a> is predominant in Vietnam, Thailand, Laos, Cambodia, Burma and Singapore. Ancestor worship and <a href="/wiki/Confucianism" title="Confucianism">Confucianism</a> are also widely practised in Vietnam and Singapore.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> is predominant in the Philippines, eastern Indonesia, East Malaysia and East Timor. The Philippines has the largest Roman Catholic population in Asia. East Timor is also predominantly Roman Catholic due to a history of Portuguese rule.\n</p><p>No individual Southeast Asian country is religiously homogeneous. Some groups are protected <i>de facto</i> by their isolation from the rest of the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-indigenous_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-indigenous-114">[114]</a></sup> In the world\'s most populous Muslim nation, Indonesia, Hinduism is dominant on islands such as <a href="/wiki/Bali" title="Bali">Bali</a>. Christianity also predominates in the rest of the part of the Philippines, <a href="/wiki/New_Guinea" title="New Guinea">New Guinea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Timor" title="Timor">Timor</a>. Pockets of Hindu population can also be found around Southeast Asia in Singapore, Malaysia etc. <a href="/wiki/Garuda" title="Garuda">Garuda</a> (Sanskrit: Garu&#7693;a), the <a href="/wiki/Phoenix_(mythology)" title="Phoenix (mythology)">phoenix</a> who is the mount (vahanam) of <a href="/wiki/Vishnu" title="Vishnu">Vishnu</a>, is a national symbol in both Thailand and Indonesia; in the Philippines, gold images of Garuda have been found on <a href="/wiki/Palawan" title="Palawan">Palawan</a>; gold images of other Hindu gods and goddesses have also been found on <a href="/wiki/Mindanao" title="Mindanao">Mindanao</a>. Balinese Hinduism is somewhat different from Hinduism practised elsewhere, as Animism and local culture is incorporated into it. Christians can also be found throughout Southeast Asia; they are in the majority in East Timor and the Philippines, Asia\'s largest Christian nation. In addition, there are also older tribal religious practices in remote areas of <a href="/wiki/Sarawak" title="Sarawak">Sarawak</a> in East Malaysia, Highland Philippines and Papua in eastern Indonesia. In Burma, Sakka (<a href="/wiki/Indra" title="Indra">Indra</a>) is revered as a <i><a href="/wiki/Nat_(spirit)" title="Nat (spirit)">nat</a></i>. In Vietnam, Mahayana Buddhism is practised, which is influenced by native animism but with strong emphasis on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ancestor_worship" title="Ancestor worship">ancestor worship</a>.\n</p><p>The religious composition for each country is as follows: Some values are taken from the <i><a href="/wiki/The_World_Factbook" title="The World Factbook">CIA World immigration, and historical colonization as well. Chinese">Mandarin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hokkien" title="Hokkien">Hokkien</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cantonese" title="Cantonese">Cantonese</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hakka" Arabic">Arabic</a>.\n<p>Indonesia has over 700 languages in over 17,000 islands across the archipelago, making Indonesia the second most linguistically diverse country on the planet,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> slightly behind Papua New Guinea. The official language of Indonesia is Indonesian (Bahasa Indonesia), widely used in educational, political, economic, and other formal situations. In daily activities and informal situations, most Indonesians speak in their local language(s). For more details, <i>see: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Indonesia" title="Languages of Indonesia">Languages of Indonesia</a></i>.\n</p>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Location_dot_red.svg/9px-Location_dot_red.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Location_dot_red.svg/12px-Location_dot_red.svg.png 2x" width="6"/></a></div></div><div style="position:absolute;top:47.232%;left:53.394%"><div style="position:absolute;left:-3px;top:-3px;line-height:0"><a href="/wiki/Bacolod" title="Bacolod"><img alt="Bacolod" data-file-height="64" data-file-width="64" decoding="async" height="6" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Location_dot_red.svg/6px-Location_dot_red.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Location_dot_red.svg/9px-Location_dot_red.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Location_dot_red.svg/12px-Location_dot_red.svg.png 2x" width="6"/></a></div><div style="font-size:90%;line-height:110%;position:absolute;width:6em;top:-0.75em;right:4px;text-align:right"><div style="display:inline;padding:1px;float:right;background-color:rgba(255, 255, 255, 0.3)">Bacolod</div></div></div><div style="position:absolute;top:38.722%;left:50.441%"><div style="position:absolute;left:-3px;top:-3px;line-height:0"><a href="/wiki/Muntinlupa" title="Southeast Asia"><img alt="Southeast Asia" data-file-height="64" data-file-width="64" decoding="async" height="6" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Location_dot_red.svg/6px-Location_dot_red.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Location_dot_red.svg/9px-Location_dot_red.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Location_dot_red.svg/12px-Location_dot_red.svg.png 2x" width="6"/></a></div></div></div><div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Southeast_Asia_location_map.svg" title="File:Southeast Asia location map.svg"> </a></div><div class="center" style="width:auto; margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;"><b>Most populous cities in Southeast Asia</b> (500,000+ inhabitants)</div></div></div></div></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Southeast_Asia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asian_cinema" title="Southeast Asian cinema">Southeast Asian cinema</a>, <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asian_Games" title="Southeast Asian Games">Southeast Asian Games</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Southeast_Asian_music" title="Southeast Asian music">Southeast Asian music</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Burmese_puppetry.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1280" data-file-width="853" decoding="async" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Burmese_puppetry.jpg/170px-Burmese_puppetry.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Burmese_puppetry.jpg/255px-Burmese_puppetry.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Burmese_puppetry.jpg/340px-Burmese_puppetry.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Burmese_puppetry.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Burmese puppet performance</div></div></div>\n<p>The culture in Southeast Asia is very diverse: on mainland Southeast Asia, the culture is a mix of Burmese, Cambodian, Laotian and Thai (<a href="/wiki/Greater_India" title="Greater India">Indian</a>) and Vietnamese (<a href="/wiki/East_Asian_cultural_sphere" title="East Asian cultural sphere">Chinese</a>) cultures. While in Indonesia, the Philippines, Singapore and Malaysia the culture is a mix of indigenous <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Austronesian_people" title="Austronesian people">Austronesian</a>, Indian, Islamic, Western, and Chinese cultures. Also Brunei shows a strong influence from Arabia. Singapore and Vietnam show more Chinese influence<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> in that Singapore, although being geographically a Southeast Asian nation, is home to a large Chinese majority and Vietnam was in <a href="/wiki/East_Asian_cultural_sphere" title="East Asian cultural sphere">China\'s sphere of influence</a> for much of its history. Indian influence in Singapore is only evident through the Tamil migrants,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> which influenced, to some extent, the cuisine of Singapore. Throughout Vietnam\'s history, it has had no direct influence from India &#8211; only through contact with the Thai, Khmer and Cham peoples.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Paddy_field,_Vietnam.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1000" data-file-width="1505" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Paddy_field%2C_Vietnam.jpg/220px-Paddy_field%2C_Vietnam.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Paddy_field%2C_Vietnam.jpg/330px-Paddy_field%2C_Vietnam.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Paddy_field%2C_Vietnam.jpg/440px-Paddy_field%2C_Vietnam.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Paddy_field,_Vietnam.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Paddy_field" title="Paddy field">paddy field</a> in Vietnam.</div></div></div>\n<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rice_paddy" title="Rice paddy">Rice paddy</a> agriculture has existed in Southeast Asia for thousands of years, ranging across the subregion. Some dramatic examples of these rice paddies populate the <a href="/wiki/Banaue_Rice_Terraces" title="Banaue Rice Terraces">Banaue Rice Terraces</a> in the mountains of Luzon in the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>. Maintenance of these paddies is very labour-intensive. The rice paddies are well-suited to the monsoon climate of the region.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Stilt_house" title="Stilt house">Stilt houses</a> can be found all over Southeast Asia, from Thailand and Vietnam, to Borneo, to Luzon in the Philippines, to <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Papua_New_Guinea_stilt_house&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Papua New Guinea stilt house (page does not exist)">Papua New Guinea</a>. The region has diverse metalworking, especially in Indonesia. This include weaponry, such as the distinctive <a href="/wiki/Kris" title="Kris">kris</a>, and musical instruments, such as the <a href="/wiki/Gamelan" title="Gamelan">gamelan</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Influences">Influences</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Southeast_Asia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Influences">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The region\'s chief cultural influences have been from some combination of <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_India" title="Culture of India">India</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Culture_of_China" title="Culture of China">China</a>. Diverse cultural influence is pronounced in the Philippines, derived particularly from the period of the Spanish and American rule, contact with Indian-influenced cultures, and the Chinese and Japanese trading era.\n</p><p>As a rule, the peoples who ate with their fingers were more likely influenced by the culture of India, for example, than the culture of China, where the peoples ate with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chopstick" title="Chopstick">chopsticks</a>; tea, as a beverage, can be found across the region. The <a href="/wiki/Fish_sauce" title="Fish sauce">fish sauces</a> distinctive to the region tend to vary.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arts">Arts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Southeast_Asia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Arts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Royal_Ballet_Camboda_Apsara_Mera.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1080" data-file-width="1520" decoding="async" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Royal_Ballet_Camboda_Apsara_Mera.jpg/220px-Royal_Ballet_Camboda_Apsara_Mera.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Royal_Ballet_Camboda_Apsara_Mera.jpg/330px-Royal_Ballet_Camboda_Apsara_Mera.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Royal_Ballet_Camboda_Apsara_Mera.jpg/440px-Royal_Ballet_Camboda_Apsara_Mera.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Royal_Ballet_Camboda_Apsara_Mera.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Royal_Ballet_of_Cambodia" title="Royal Ballet of Cambodia">Royal Ballet of Cambodia</a> (Paris, France 2010)</div></div></div>\n<p>The arts of Southeast Asia have affinity with the arts of other areas. Dance in much of Southeast Asia includes movement of the hands as well as the feet, to express the dance\'s emotion and meaning of the story that the ballerina is going to tell the audience. Most of Southeast Asia introduced dance into their court; in particular, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Khmer_classical_dance" title="Khmer classical dance">Cambodian royal ballet</a> represented them in the early 7th century before the <a href="/wiki/Khmer_Empire" title="Khmer Empire">Khmer Empire</a>, which was highly influenced by Indian Hinduism. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Apsara_Dance" title="Apsara Dance">Apsara Dance</a>, famous for strong hand and feet movement, is a great example of Hindu symbolic dance.\n</p><p>Puppetry and shadow plays were also a favoured form of entertainment in past centuries, a famous one being <a href="/wiki/Wayang" title="Wayang">Wayang</a> from Indonesia. The arts and literature in some of Southeast Asia is quite influenced by Hinduism, which was brought to them centuries ago. Indonesia, despite conversion to Islam which opposes certain forms of art, has retained many forms of Hindu-influenced practices, culture, art and literature. An example is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wayang_Kulit" title="Wayang Kulit">Wayang Kulit</a> (Shadow Puppet) and literature like the <a href="/wiki/Ramayana" title="Ramayana">Ramayana</a>. The wayang kulit show has been recognized by <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> on November 7, 2003, as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Masterpiece_of_Oral_and_Intangible_Heritage_of_Humanity" title="Masterpiece of Oral and Intangible Heritage of Humanity">Masterpiece of Oral and Intangible Heritage of Humanity</a>.\n</p><p>It has been pointed out that Khmer and Indonesian classical arts were concerned with depicting the life of the gods, but to the Southeast Asian mind the life of the gods was the life of the peoples themselves&#8212;joyous, earthy, yet divine. The <a href="/wiki/Tai_peoples" title="Tai peoples">Tai</a>, coming late into Southeast Asia, brought with them some Chinese artistic traditions, but they soon shed them in favour of the Khmer and <a href="/wiki/Mon_people" title="Mon people">Mon</a> traditions, and the only indications of their earlier contact with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Culture_of_China" title="Culture of China">Chinese</a> arts were in the style of their temples, especially the tapering roof, and in their <a href="/wiki/Lacquerware" title="Lacquerware">lacquerware</a>.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Southeast_Asia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Southeast_Asia" title="Music of Southeast Asia">Music of Southeast Asia</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Angklung-arumba.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="981" data-file-width="905" decoding="async" height="238" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Angklung-arumba.jpg/220px-Angklung-arumba.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Angklung-arumba.jpg/330px-Angklung-arumba.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Angklung-arumba.jpg/440px-Angklung-arumba.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Angklung-arumba.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Angklung" title="Angklung">Angklung</a> as a <a href="/wiki/Masterpieces_of_the_Oral_and_Intangible_Heritage_of_Humanity" title="Masterpieces of the Oral and Intangible Heritage of Humanity">Masterpiece of Oral and Intangible Heritage of Humanity</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Traditional music in Southeast Asia is as varied as its many ethnic and cultural divisions. Main styles of traditional music can be seen: Court music, folk music, music styles of smaller ethnic groups, and music influenced by genres outside the geographic region.\n</p><p>Of the court and folk genres, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gong-chime" title="Gong-chime">gong-chime</a> ensembles and orchestras make up the majority (the exception being lowland areas of Vietnam). <i><a href="/wiki/Gamelan" title="Gamelan">Gamelan</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Angklung" title="Angklung">Angklung</a></i> orchestras from <i><a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Piphat" title="Piphat">Piphat</a></i> /<i><a href="/wiki/Pinpeat" title="Pinpeat">Pinpeat</a></i> ensembles of Thailand and Cambodia and the <i><a href="/wiki/Kulintang" title="Kulintang">Kulintang</a></i> ensembles of the southern Philippines, <a href="/wiki/Borneo" title="Borneo">Borneo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sulawesi" title="Sulawesi">Sulawesi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Timor" title="Timor">Timor</a> are the three main distinct styles of musical genres that have influenced other traditional musical styles in the region. String instruments also are popular in the region.\n</p><p>On November 18, 2010, UNESCO officially recognized angklung as a <i>Masterpiece of Oral and Intangible Heritage of Humanity</i>, and encourage Indonesian people and government to safeguard, transmit, promote performances and to encourage the craftsmanship of angklung making.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Writing">Writing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Southeast_Asia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Writing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Writing_systems_of_Southeast_Asia" title="Writing systems of Southeast Asia">Writing systems of Southeast Asia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baybayin" title="Baybayin">Baybayin</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jawi_script" title="Jawi script">Jawi script</a>, <a href="/wiki/S.E.A._Write_Award" title="S.E.A. Write Award">S.E.A. Write Award</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Thai_alphabet" title="Thai alphabet">Thai alphabet</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Thai_manuscript_Jim_Thompson_Museum_IMG_7170.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2432" data-file-width="3954" decoding="async" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Thai_manuscript_Jim_Thompson_Museum_IMG_7170.jpg/220px-Thai_manuscript_Jim_Thompson_Museum_IMG_7170.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Thai_manuscript_Jim_Thompson_Museum_IMG_7170.jpg/330px-Thai_manuscript_Jim_Thompson_Museum_IMG_7170.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Thai_manuscript_Jim_Thompson_Museum_IMG_7170.jpg/440px-Thai_manuscript_Jim_Thompson_Museum_IMG_7170.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Thai_manuscript_Jim_Thompson_Museum_IMG_7170.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thai_script" title="Thai script">Thai</a> manuscript from before the 19th-century writing system.</div></div></div>\n<p>The history of Southeast Asia has led to a wealth of different authors, from both within and without writing about the region.\n</p><p>Originally, <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_India" title="Culture of India">Indians</a> were the ones who taught the native inhabitants about writing. This is shown through <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brahmic_family" title="Brahmic family">Brahmic</a> forms of writing present in the region such as the <a href="/wiki/Balinese_script" title="Balinese script">Balinese script</a> shown on split palm leaf called <i>lontar</i> (see image to the left &#8212; magnify the image to see the writing on the flat side, and the decoration on the reverse side).\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pura_Puseh_05153.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="682" data-file-width="909" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Pura_Puseh_05153.jpg/220px-Pura_Puseh_05153.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Pura_Puseh_05153.jpg/330px-Pura_Puseh_05153.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Pura_Puseh_05153.jpg/440px-Pura_Puseh_05153.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pura_Puseh_05153.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sign in <a href="/wiki/Balinese_script" title="Balinese script">Balinese</a> and <a href="/wiki/Latin_script" title="Latin script">Latin</a> script at a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hindu" title="Hindu">Hindu</a> temple in <a href="/wiki/Bali" title="Bali">Bali</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The antiquity of this form of writing extends before the invention of paper around the year 100 in China. Note each palm leaf section was only several lines, written longitudinally across the leaf, and bound by twine to the other sections. The outer portion was decorated. The alphabets of Southeast Asia tended to be <a href="/wiki/Abugida" title="Abugida">abugidas</a>, until the arrival of the Europeans, who used words that also ended in consonants, not just vowels. Other forms of official documents, which did not use paper, included Javanese copperplate scrolls. This material would have been more durable than paper in the tropical climate of Southeast Asia.\n</p><p>In Malaysia, Brunei, and Singapore, the Malay language is now generally written in the Latin script. The same phenomenon is present in Indonesian, although different spelling standards are utilised (e.g. \'Teksi\' in Malay and \'Taksi\' in Indonesian for the word \'Taxi\').\n</p><p>The use of Chinese characters, in the past and present, is only evident in Vietnam and more recently, Singapore and Malaysia. The adoption of Chinese characters in Vietnam dates back to around 111BC, when it was occupied by the Chinese. A Vietnamese script called <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chu_nom" title="Chu nom">Chu nom</a> used modified Chinese characters to express the Vietnamese language. Both classical Chinese and Chu Nom were used up until the early 20th century.\n</p><p>However, the use of the Chinese script has been in decline, especially in Singapore and Malaysia as the younger generations are in favour of the Latin Script.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Southeast_Asia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div aria-label="Portals"
